          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

1. Checkout

https://pdfium.googlesource.com/pdfium/+/877b5b9170f101e4aec980e3807dbb787a3f6fa4

Looked into this with cbruni@ a bit now and it looks like a missed generational barrier from IC code.



<span class="line"><!---->Looked into this with cbruni@ a bit now and it looks like a missed generational barrier from IC code.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





What we know:



<span class="line"><!---->What we know:<!----></span>



<br>





- JSArray with holey elements where elements are backed by a FixedArray in OLD_SPACE



<span class="line"><!---->- JSArray with holey elements where elements are backed by a FixedArray in OLD_SPACE<!----></span>



<br>





- JSArrayBuffer in new space



<span class="line"><!---->- JSArrayBuffer in new space<!----></span>



<br>





- Previously slot pointed into RO SPACE (odd ball)



<span class="line"><!---->- Previously slot pointed into RO SPACE (odd ball)<!----></span>



<br>





- We write FixedArray[x] = JSArrayBuffer



<span class="line"><!---->- We write FixedArray[x] = JSArrayBuffer<!----></span>



<br>





- On this interesting write we seem to fail in the OutOfLineRecordWrite [1] page check where we should see the new space page having the kPointersToHereAreInteresting bit set. However, we see that it has kPointersFromHereAreInteresting are set.



<span class="line"><!---->- On this interesting write we seem to fail in the OutOfLineRecordWrite [1] page check where we should see the new space page having the kPointersToHereAreInteresting bit set. However, we see that it has kPointersFromHereAreInteresting are set.<!----></span>



<br>





- This results in us bailing out on the write barrier.



<span class="line"><!---->- This results in us bailing out on the write barrier.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The only related change I remember now was [2]. Locally reverting didn't help though, so it's not that.



<span class="line"><!---->The only related change I remember now was [2]. Locally reverting didn't help though, so it's not that.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Looking into why we set up wrong page flags now. 



<span class="line"><!---->Looking into why we set up wrong page flags now. <!----></span>

Components

:

<strong><!---->Components:</strong>


          


          

Blink>JavaScript>Compiler


          




          

<br>


        




        




      

<div class="issue-diff">
        <!---->
          <strong><!---->Components:</strong>
          
          Blink&gt;JavaScript&gt;Compiler
          
          <br>
        <!---->
        
      </div>

<br>


    


        


      


        









The issue here is very subtle: PDFium builds without wasm [1] and unfortunately this configuration has a bug in the compiler when emitting the trampolines for write barriers on x86. So the bug is limited to a configuration of x86 without wasm at build time.



<span class="line"><!---->The issue here is very subtle: PDFium builds without wasm [1] and unfortunately this configuration has a bug in the compiler when emitting the trampolines for write barriers on x86. So the bug is limited to a configuration of x86 without wasm at build time.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Afaik, there is no Chrome build shipping in this config, so I guess this is a PDFium-only issue. I don't think the configuration is tested well as our regular V8-based CF should immediately find an issue when running without write barriers from generated code.



<span class="line"><!---->Afaik, there is no Chrome build shipping in this config, so I guess this is a PDFium-only issue. I don't think the configuration is tested well as our regular V8-based CF should immediately find an issue when running without write barriers from generated code.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Fix is in flight here: 



<span class="line"><!---->Fix is in flight here: <!----></span>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/v8/v8/+/3236990



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/v8/v8/+/3236990"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/v8/v8/+/3236990<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





The larger question is whether this actually needs a backmerge.



<span class="line"><!---->The larger question is whether this actually needs a backmerge.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





tsepez: Is x86+JS a valid PDFium config? I guess on Windows 32bit?



<span class="line"><!---->tsepez: Is x86+JS a valid PDFium config? I guess on Windows 32bit?<!----></span>

v8_enable_webassembly was introduced for the Cobalt team to reduce binary size and lower the maintenance effort for them. It has not been intended to be supported beyond that until now. If there is more use of that flag, we should take the necessary steps to feel comfortable supporting it.



<span class="line"><!---->v8_enable_webassembly was introduced for the Cobalt team to reduce binary size and lower the maintenance effort for them. It has not been intended to be supported beyond that until now. If there is more use of that flag, we should take the necessary steps to feel comfortable supporting it.<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.



<span class="line"><!---->Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.<!----></span>

We would like to award you $1000 for this report and your efforts. A member of our finance team will be in touch soon to arrange payment. Thank you!
